<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="implementation-of-the-imci-strategy-involves-the-following-three-components">Implementation of the IMCI strategy involves the following three components:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#implementation-of-the-imci-strategy-involves-the-following-three-components" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Improvements in the case management skills of health staff through the provision of locally adapted guidelines on IMCI and activities to promote their use</li>
<li>Improvements in the health care system required for effective management of childhood illnesses</li>
<li>Improvements in family and community practices</li>
</ul>
<p>The objective of IMCI is not to takeover the responsibilities of the various programmes, but to ensure that the activities are well coordinated and effectively implemented in order to contribute to IMCI.</p>
<p>Remember we have already covered some interventions currently included in IMCI strategy.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-3-nutrition-and-nutritional-disorders-in-children">SECTION 3: NUTRITION AND NUTRITIONAL DISORDERS IN CHILDREN<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-nutrition-and-nutritional-disorders-in-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You are already conversant with the various types of foods used in Kenyan society and their nutritive value as well as how they vary from one ethnic group to another and from one religious group to another. However different they may be, the common denominator is that they provide us with all the nutrients we need for our bodily functions.</p>
<p>You learnt earlier in this unit of the importance of nutrition in growth and development and general health maintenance. You will look at the known food constituents available for human consumption.</p>
<p>You will now look at the objectives for this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the groups of foods, their nutritive value and explain their functions in the human body</li>
<li>Describe various nutritional disorders in children</li>
<li>Describe the management of children with common nutritional disorders</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-nutrients-and-their-functions">Food Nutrients and Their Functions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-nutrients-and-their-functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Think of all the major food groups their functions. Write them down on a piece of paper then compare your thoughts with the information that will be covered on the forthcoming pages.</p>
<p>You will now look at each of most common food groups and their functions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="proteins">Proteins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#proteins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are a group of foods that supply amino acids for the growth and repair of body tissue. Proteins play a very important role in immunity, the blood clotting mechanism, transport of body substances and the regulation and maintenance of osmotic pressure. Therefore, a good amount of protein should be given to patients, especially children. When taken into the body, proteins are broken down to amino acids, which are then absorbed into the blood stream via the villi so as to be utilised by the body.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Sources of Proteins</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Animal Proteins</td><td>Plant Proteins</td></tr><tr><td>Meat, Chicken, Fish, Milk, Eggs, Cheese</td><td>Peas, Groundnuts, Beans, Fruits, Lentils, Vegetables</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="carbohydrates">Carbohydrates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#carbohydrates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are the main energy source for the body. When eaten and absorbed into the bloodstream in its simplest form, carbohydrate is referred to as glucose. Glucose is very important for the brain and nerve function. Carbohydrates can further be divided into three main categories, that is, sugar, starch and polysaccharides</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-carbohydrates">sources of carbohydrates<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-carbohydrates" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Carbohydrates can be obtained from potatoes, rice, ugali, fruits, milk, cereals, starches and vegetables. Some carbohydrates form indigestible polysaccharides and cellulose, which form roughage essential for the stimulation of intestinal peristalsis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fats">Fats<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fats" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Although fats have a higher caloric value, they are less efficiently utilised by the brain and nerve tissue. However, fats are the body's largest energy store. Fat is found under the skin and around some body organs, such as the kidneys to give support and protection from injuries. Other functions include formation of cholesterol and steroid hormones. They are also vehicles for the absorption of vitamins A, B, E and K. They are usually broken down to fatty acids and glycerols before being absorbed into the bloodstream via intestinal villi and lacteal vessels. Fats are available in fatty meat, chicken, fish, butter, milk and vegetable oils and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamins">Vitamins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are organic compounds which are classified as water soluble and fat soluble vitamins. The water soluble vitamins are B and C while fat soluble include A, D, E and K. All the vitamins are obtained through food consumption. Vitamin D can be synthesised</p>
<p>through the action of sunlight and vitamin K, which itself is synthesised by the large intestinal bacteria.</p>
<p>Fat soluble vitamins are found in fish, meat, milk, butter and plant oils. They can easily be stored in the liver and adipose tissue. Over consumption of fat can lead to hypervitaminosis, though that is a rare occurrence. Deficiency in fat soluble vitamins is rare but if it occurs, it is usually due to trauma or severe illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mineral-salts">Mineral Salts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mineral-salts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main mineral salts include sodium, potassium, calcium, magnesium, chlorine and sulphur. Only small amounts of each mineral are required to sustain bodily functions. They are essential for enzyme components. Those of significant nutritional value are iron, zinc, and iodine. Iron deficiency leads to anaemia, while iodine deficiency leads to goitre. Zinc is also required for enzyme reaction, especially during growth and wound healing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water">Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the major component of the body and the dietary intake must have sufficient quantity in order to meet daily needs. Without adequate amounts of water, the body tissues cannot function properly. Water is the solvent for cellular changes. Water acts as a medium for ions, and transports nutrients and waste products. It is also important for the regulation of body temperature. The amount required varies from one person to another, though in adults an average of two to three litres should be taken daily. In children, the amount will vary according to the age.</p>
<p>Having covered the importance of nutrition, you shall now proceed to the causes, diagnosis and management of various nutritional disorders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-nutrition">Sources of Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Nutrient</th><th>Source samples</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Animal protein</td><td>Meat, chicken, fish, milk, eggs, cheese</td></tr><tr><td>Plant protein</td><td>Peas, groundnuts, beans, fruits, lentils, vegetables</td></tr><tr><td>Carbohydrates</td><td>Potatoes, rice, ugali, fruits, milk, cereals, and vegetables</td></tr><tr><td>Fat</td><td>Fats are available in fatty meat, chicken, fish,</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>butter, milk and vegetable oils</td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin A (retinol, retinaldehyde, retinoic acid)</td><td>Carrots</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin B1 = thiamin</td><td>Potato, meat such as beef</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin B2 = riboflavin</td><td>Beef liver, dairy produce</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin B6 = pyridoxine, pyridoxal, pyridoxamine</td><td>Potatoes, fish</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin B12 = cobalamine</td><td>Dairy produce, eggs</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin C = ascorbic acid</td><td>Fruit such as orange, lemons, tangerines</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin D = calciferol</td><td>Sunlight, tuna fish</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin E = tocopherol, tocotrienol</td><td>Spinach, sunflower seeds, walnuts</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin K = phylloquinone</td><td>Sprouts, cabbage, cheese</td></tr><tr><td>Vitamin C = ascorbic acid</td><td>Sodium, potassium, calcium, magnesium, chlorine and sulphur</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nutritional-disorders">Nutritional Disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutritional-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should have learnt a lot about nutrition both in your secondary school and in the basic nursing course. Nutritional disorders are conditions occurring in one's body as a result of bad nutrition or malnutrition.</p>
<p>Malnutrition is more than a medical problem. It is brought about by dysfunctions in economic, demographic, cultural religious and ecological processes. Malnutrition may be due to an excess, deficit or imbalance in the essential components of a balanced diet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="over-nutrition">Over Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#over-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This refers to ingestion of more food than is required for the body needs, as may be seen in the case of obesity. This condition is more common in rich western countries (the developed world).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="under-nutrition">Under Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#under-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This describes a state of poor nourishment as a result of inadequate diet or presence of disease, which interferes with the normal appetite,</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>absorption and assimilation of ingested food. Inadequate or poor nourishment diet is more prevalent in the third world countries that are still developing and poor. Included in under nutrition are protein energy malnutrition and vitamin deficiencies.</p>
<p>The main causes of under nutrition are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Insufficient food resources</li>
<li>Lack of education about nutritional needs</li>
<li>Poor socioeconomic conditions</li>
<li>Chronic illnesses</li>
</ul>
<p>You should have learnt a lot about nutrition both in your secondary school and in the basic nursing course. Nutritional disorders are conditions occurring in one's body as a result of bad nutrition or malnutrition.</p>
<p>Malnutrition is more than a medical problem. It is brought about by dysfunctions in economic, demographic, cultural religious and ecological processes. Malnutrition may be due to an excess, deficit or imbalance in the essential components of a balanced diet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protein-energy-malnutrition-pem">Protein Energy Malnutrition (PEM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protein-energy-malnutrition-pem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This condition is also referred to as protein calorie malnutrition (PCM). It is the most common form of under nutrition in children. Protein Calorie Malnutrition can be classified as primary type, which means the nutritional needs are not met as a result of poor eating habits, or secondary type, which refers to malnutrition occurring as a result of an alteration or defect in ingestion, absorption or metabolism. In such circumstances, the tissue needs are not met even though the dietary intake would be deemed satisfactory under normal conditions, for example in diseases such as measles, tuberculosis, mal-absorption syndromes and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-forms-of-protein-energy-malnutrition">Clinical Forms of Protein Energy Malnutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-forms-of-protein-energy-malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The two clinical forms of protein energy malnutrition are kwashiorkor and marasmus. In kwashiorkor the main deficient nutrient is protein, while in marasmus the deficiency is caloric. There are some children who fall in between the two forms, and who suffer growth failure but exhibit no signs of either disease. Both conditions impair growth and if they are chronic will end up reducing the size of an individual</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kwashiorkor">Kwashiorkor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kwashiorkor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this condition there is a lack in protein relative to calories, often associated with a normal growth pattern until six to eight months of age when the weight of the child begins to decrease. The name originated from a local Ghanaian language meaning 'displayed child'. Characteristics include growth retardation, changes in skin tone, mental apathy and other bodily changes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Kwashiorkor may be caused by a sudden change from breast milk to porridge, which is entirely comprised of carbohydrates. This sudden change in feeding habits may be prompted if the mother realises that she is pregnant while still breast feeding.</li>
<li>Infections, such as malaria, measles and so on, accompanied by fever which tends to use up the scarce protein stored in the body may result in kwashiorkor.</li>
<li>Anorexia, due to other illnesses, and intestinal worms, which draw on the child's food supply, may also be predisposing factors. The onset is commonest between one to three years but may extend to five years.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following are some of the clinical features of kwashiorkor:</p>
<ul>
<li>Growth failure and some muscle wasting</li>
<li>Oedema of the face, hands, anus, feet and bulging abdomen</li>
<li>The hair becomes thin, straight and brownish in colour</li>
<li>The child has poor appetite and is irritable</li>
<li>There is mental apathy and lack of interest in the surroundings</li>
<li>Diarrhoea</li>
<li>Hepatomegaly and anaemia</li>
</ul>
<p>When undertaking diagnostic investigations, you should carry out the following procedures:</p>
<ul>
<li>First, you should always take the child's personal history from the parents.</li>
<li>Secondly, physical and laboratory examinations to exclude infections such as malaria which is done by testing blood slide for malarial parasites and intestinal worms which are checked from the stool (ova and cysts).</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Thirdly, blood tests for WBC and haemoglobin estimation should exclude anaemia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marasmus">Marasmus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marasmus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The term marasmus refers to starvation. The disease is caused by lack of food of any kind, which includes proteins, carbohydrates, fats and vitamins. Marasmus occurs at any age, but is more commonly found in infants who do not get enough breast feeding or during the weaning period, when poor bottle feeding practices are followed or supplementary foods are not given.</p>
<p>Clinical features of marasmus include:</p>
<ul>
<li>The weight of the affected child normally drops to 60% below the standard expected weight</li>
<li>Muscular atrophy, especially visible on the arms and legs, with loss of subcutaneous fat and legs and arms are thin</li>
<li>Wrinkled, thin and flaccid skin</li>
<li>The face of the child usually looks old and anxious</li>
<li>The child may have diarrhoea or constipation</li>
<li>The child has very good appetite when being fed but does not put on weight</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="marasmic-kwashiorkor">Marasmic Kwashiorkor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#marasmic-kwashiorkor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="how-would-you-identify-this-condition-in-a-child">How would you identify this condition in a child?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-would-you-identify-this-condition-in-a-child" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Any child with kwashiorkor has some muscle wasting and loss of subcutaneous fat, regardless of the presence of oedema. If this process is severe enough to result in weight loss below 60% of the normal expected weight according to their age, then the child is said to have marasmic kwashiorkor.</p>
<p>There are several factors, which contribute to protein energy malnutrition (PEM). Many people in developing countries know very little about the nutritional values of the food they eat. In addition, some people in the developing countries are traditionalists and the food they consume is often dictated by cultural norms. For example, there may be customs outlining what men, women and children are supposed to eat and what they are forbidden.</p>
<p>Poverty is also an important factor. Most body building foodstuffs suitable for weaning, for example, milk and eggs, are too expensive for a large percentage of the population. This factor often pre-disposes parents to act in a seemingly negligent manner, especially in instances where they are pre-occupied by income generating activities, leaving the child in the care of other people who may not be aware of the child's dietary requirements.</p>
<p>Poor farming practices, and natural disasters, like droughts and floods may also lead to a loss in income and inability to meet the dietary requirements of the child. Finally, political instability often drives people away from their natural environment to camps (as refugees), where they are unable to engage in productive activities and may have no means of supplementing their basic rations.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-8c677e47.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-children-suffering-from-pem">Management of Children Suffering from PEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-children-suffering-from-pem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="protein-energy-malnutrition-pem">Protein Energy Malnutrition (PEM)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protein-energy-malnutrition-pem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Mild nutritional problems are easy to deal with and pose no major problems to you, as a nurse. The moderate and severe types of protein energy malnutrition (PEM) must be investigated to enable the health care worker to establish the origin or cause of malnutrition in different children.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 252 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="investigations">Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The following investigations should be carried out:</p>
<ul>
<li>Take the family and social history to identify the cause of malnourishment e.g. enquire into the type of food used at home, the child's appetite and other relevant points to that effect.</li>
<li>Conduct a physical examination to find out if the child is suffering from any other health problems. Weigh the child, take the height and head/limb circumferences and record them.</li>
<li>A blood test for white blood cells, haemoglobin and malarial parasites should also be conducted.</li>
<li>A stool test should be carried out to exclude the possibility of intestinal worms.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-pem">Management of PEM<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-pem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The immediate requirement for a child suffering from PEM is energy. In the presence of an oedema, the energy requirement is 100 calories/kg body weight/day. In a marasmic child, or when oedema has subsided, then 150-200 calories/kg body weight/day is the recommended caloric intake.</p>
<p>You should assess whether the child is able to consume food orally. If this is not deemed possible, then a naso-gastric tube should be inserted for feeding purposes. If the child is very sick, cold or collapsed, then they should be hospitalised and an IV infusion of glucose should be commenced. Any infection should be managed with appropriate antibiotics. The child should be kept warm and a doctor has to be called urgently.</p>
<p>Severe cases should be tube fed. You should begin with milk products, which may have to be diluted. These should have added sugar and vitamins. As the condition of the patient improves, undiluted milk, sugar, oil and vitamins should be given. Other staple foods should be gradually introduced.</p>
<p>A high calorie feed should be commenced after two to four days, with solids being cautiously and slowly introduced. As the condition of the child gradually improves the feeding tube should be removed and a cup or a cup and spoon should be used to feed the child. The parent/guardian should be involved in the feeding of their child under the supervision of the nursing staff.</p>
<p>Feeds should initially be given at two to three hour intervals and later, as the child's condition improves, the quantity of food should be increased and given after every four hours. The amount and composition of food administered should be worked out by the doctor and nutritionist or dietician. The amount given each time must be documented on the fluid and feeding chart. Urine output must also be strictly monitored.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vitamin-deficiencies">Vitamin Deficiencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamin-deficiencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Vitamin deficiency diseases commonly occur in association with protein energy malnutrition (PEM). Severely malnourished children are, therefore, likely to suffer from deficiencies of various vitamins, which will have to be added into the diet as part of management of malnutrition. With the normal balanced diet supplemented by an additional intake of protective foods such as greens, vegetables and fruits, the deficiencies will be prevented.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vitamin-a-deficiency">Vitamin A Deficiency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamin-a-deficiency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Vitamin A plays a number of important roles. It combines with specific proteins to form the retinal pigments called rhodopsin and iodopsin. These are essential for vision in dim light. It is necessary for the development of bones and teeth and essential in the formation and maturation of epithelia of the skin, eyes and other body systems such as digestive, respiratory and reproductive tracts. It also helps to build body resistance against illness, promotes good health, helps growth and development and finally improves eyesight.</p>
<p>Children between the ages of zero to six years are among the risk group of people who are prone to deficiency.</p>
<p>Several foodstuffs are rich in this vitamin. They include breast milk, other milk, dark leafy vegetables, carrots, eggs, meat, fish and fortified foods such as blue band margarine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-include">Clinical Features Include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Reversible dryness of the conjunctiva and the cornea, exophthalmia in the early stages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Night blindness during early stages</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keratomalacia, irreversible corneal damage with scarring or rupture of the eyeball, this causes impaired eyesight (blindness)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bitot's spots (white 'foamy' areas) often seen near the lateral part of the sclera of the eye</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Vitamin A deficiency can be treated by administering 200, 000 i.u. orally. Start a second dose the following day. Administer a third and fourth dose of 200,000 i.u. orally one to four weeks later. In children below the age of 12 months, the vitamin A dosage is halved.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamin-b-deficiency">Vitamin B Deficiency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamin-b-deficiency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This vitamin is referred to as vitamin B complex because it consists of various factors naturally occurring together. The deficiency of one factor is uncommon.</p>
<p>A deficiency in vitamin B1 (Thiamine or Aneurine) is usually associated with a polished rice diet. It is relatively uncommon on the African continent, but where it does occur the child suffers from beriberi characterised by muscle weakness, which may lead to cardiac failure.</p>
<p>Vitamin B2 (Riboflavin) deficiencies lead to mucous membrane lesions resulting in dry cracked lips, glossitis and stomatitis.</p>
<p>Nicotinic acid deficiency is a problem that mainly affects adults. It is also known as pellagra.</p>
<p>Folic acid (folate) deficiencies are rare in children, though common in pregnancy and other conditions, such as recurrent haemolytic anaemias and malaria where the demand to manufacture RBC is great. A lack of vitamin B12 may be a contributing factor to anaemia.</p>
<p>The treatment of vitamin B deficiencies usually involves vitamin B complex in the form of Multivite, most commonly through oral administration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamin-c-deficiency">Vitamin C Deficiency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamin-c-deficiency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vitamin C (Ascorbic acid) is readily found in green vegetable, fruits and fruit juices. It is useful in increasing iron absorption from the intestine to the blood stream and in the promotion of wound healing. A deficiency in vitamin C leads to scurvy. It occurs in children between six to sixteen months of age. Scurvy is characterised by haemorrhages in the skin, gums and under the periosteum of long bones, which become very painful.</p>
<p>Treatment involves a course of ascorbic acid tablets, which are quite easily available. Vegetables, fruits and fruit juices are also useful to prevent deficiencies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamin-d-deficiency">Vitamin D Deficiency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamin-d-deficiency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vitamin D is essential for the development of strong bones and teeth. A deficiency in this vitamin affects the epithelial structures of the skin, the mucous membrane and eye.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-forms-of-vitamin-deficiencies">Clinical Forms of Vitamin Deficiencies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-forms-of-vitamin-deficiencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are of two types namely rickets and osteomalacia. The two terms need to be well defined in order to understand the difference between them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rickets">Rickets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rickets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rickets can be described as a failure in the mineralisation of rapidly growing bone or osteoid tissue. It occurs mostly in infants, toddlers and adolescents and is mainly a result of vitamin deficiencies. Childhood active rickets normally occurs when the diet lacks adequate vitamin D, which is essential for the metabolism of calcium and phosphorus necessary for good growth of bones.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-03942547.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-314c6f2a.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="osteomalacia">Osteomalacia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#osteomalacia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Osteomalacia is defined as a failure in the mineralisation of the mature bone. It occurs in adults whose bones are already fully grown.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are several factors that predispose to rickets. Premature babies are often predisposed because the deposits of calcium and phosphorus at birth are inadequate for the infant's rapid growth. Hereditary factors can also be crucial, for instance, dark skinned people tend to block the ultra-violet light that triggers vitamin D production leading to insufficient quantities of the aforementioned vitamin. Conversely, a failure to expose infants to sunlight may also result in deficiencies.</p>
<p>Soon after birth, the infant receives vitamin D from the mother. If the mother does not breastfeed adequately the baby may soon become deficient of vitamin D. Similarly, if the mother continues to breastfeed but her own intake of this vitamin is inadequate then the baby will still suffer from a deficiency. Cultural or religious beliefs, for example, vegetarianism, may also lead to vitamin D deficiencies if the child is not exposed to adequate milk and milk products or their substitutes.</p>
<p>Malabsorption, is another factor that must be taken into account when trying to determine the cause of the vitamin D deficiency. The infant may have certain diseases, such as celiac</p>
<p>disease, which may interfere with, or prevent the absorption of vitamin D and calcium from the gut. Diseases of the parathyroid glands or any of those which interfere with calcium and phosphorus metabolism may also be predisposing factors, although these occur mainly in adults.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-68752851.jpeg" alt="img-4.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Calcitonin and parathyroid hormones together maintain plasma calcium homeostasis. When the intake of calcium and vitamin D are deficient, demineralisation of bones will occur in order to preserve calcium ion level to 9-11mg/100mls of blood (2.25-2.26mmol/litre).</p>
<p>Secondary effects include the bone changes of rickets and lowered serum phosphorus concentration. The latter is a result of parthormone, which decreases phosphorus reabsorption in the kidneys. This action elevates serum phosphatase.</p>
<p>To read about the treatment of this condition click the links below:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-of-rickets">Clinical Features of Rickets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-rickets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The extent of manifestation of rickets will depend on the age at which it occurs in the child, but it is most noticeable in the first or second year of life.</p>
<p>The following features are normally observed:</p>
<ul>
<li>On the head, the anterior fontanel takes longer than usual to close while the cranium appear soft</li>
<li>Dentition is also delayed and teeth are defective when they grow</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>There is apparent forward projection of the sternum on the chest and there is a tendency to respiratory tract infections</li>
<li>The pelvic bones may become flattened. This may eventually lead to obstetric problems in girls in their reproductive age</li>
<li>The abdomen may protrude</li>
<li>Sweating, diarrhoea and vomiting may occasionally be present</li>
<li>The child is often miserable and sleeps less at night</li>
<li>Tetany and carpopedal spasm may sometimes be present</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-investigations">Diagnostic investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Begin with a compilation of the personal history to find out the types and food content the child is given.</li>
<li>Blood for electrolytes is taken paying particular attention to calcium and phosphorus levels.</li>
<li>An x-ray of wrists should be taken showing widening of distal end of the ulna and radius.</li>
<li>The bone end density is decreased.</li>
<li>Do not forget to take a urine specimen for calcium and phosphorus level.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-management-of-rickets-and-preventative-care">The Management of Rickets and Preventative Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-management-of-rickets-and-preventative-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rickets can be cured in any stage. Management consists of giving an adequate amount of vitamin D and minerals in the diet. This should include plenty of milk and dairy products, eggs, green vegetables, meat and fish. Vitamin D supplements should be continued daily at the dose of 500-50,000 I.V., either orally or by intramuscular injection. The child should be exposed to sunlight daily. The parents should be advised to avoid the use of thick nappies, as these tend to bow the femur by separating them. The infant should be nursed flat on a hard mattress during the acute stage with restriction of walking or crawling. Where splints are used to correct the bowing, care should be taken to prevent sores. In a few cases surgical intervention may be required. Above all, rehabilitative care is essential.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-care">Preventive Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One of the simplest preventive measures is to expose babies to sunlight for a few hours a day. This will ensure the infant has a sufficient supply of vitamin D. All babies up to the age of five years should be given a well balanced diet, which includes vitamin D supplements. Health education should be extended to schools so that all members of the community who interact with children on a regular basis can observe and take the necessary action when they notice changes in the children's postures</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-a14bc6a1.jpeg" alt="img-5.jpeg">
Knock Knees</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-309a4394.jpeg" alt="img-6.jpeg">
Bow Legs</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="iodine-deficiency">Iodine Deficiency<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iodine-deficiency" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In normal circumstances, infants who are breast fed receive a thyroid hormone in the mother's milk which is sufficient to compensate for their own deficiency. They are therefore protected against mental retardation and neurological problems, which are common clinical manifestations of iodine deficiency. This is necessary until they are introduced to a solid diet. During the weaning period the mother's thyroid hormone supply to the infant becomes inadequate. Similarly breast feeding mothers who lack adequate iodine in their dietary intake may end up with infants with hypothyroidism.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Infants should be kept warm and comfortable because they tend to feel cold. You should provide the necessary care to prevent the skin from breaking. The parents should be given health education about the need for the child to maintain life long use of thyroid medication. The infant's vital signs should be monitored and a general physical observation for manifestations such as diarrhoea, vomiting, sweating, weight loss, insomnia and personality changes, which</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>may emerge with the drug treatment prescribed, should be observed. Oral replacement therapy should be employed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obesity">Obesity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obesity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Obesity in children is an important issue because if it is not monitored it may be a problem in adult life. It causes complications of the heart thereby reducing life expectancy. Over nutrition increases growth and the onset of puberty. The child may be teased and develop a poor self image, which affects self confidence, particularly when it comes to establishing relationships with the opposite sex. Obese children often require psychological support to overcome their problems.</p>
<p>You should emphasise the importance of weight reduction in the obese child although you should note that it is very difficult to achieve this in children, because a low energy diet is likely to interfere with the child's activities. The family should be asked to alter their dietary intake to accommodate what the child requires. A reduced calorie intake should be recommended, starting with one or two energy dense foods per day with an emphasis on increasing low calorie food intake. They should be educated about the medical complications of obesity so that they can make informed decision. Involve all the family members in the education programme</p>
<p>Families should be encouraged to reduce inactivity in children by limiting television and computer games, encouraging children to walk instead of being driven to and from schools and to play more actively with friends. Families should try to take a minimum of at least</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-complications-can-you-think-of-that-are-associated-with-obesity">What complications can you think of that are associated with obesity?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-complications-can-you-think-of-that-are-associated-with-obesity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Orthopaedic, that is, tibia vara (bow legs) and slipped femoral epiphysis</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Benign intracranial hypertension, which manifests with headaches and blurred optic disc margins</p>

<p>Hypertension</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="renal-osteodystrophy">Renal Osteodystrophy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#renal-osteodystrophy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a syndrome of the skeletal change found in chronic renal failure. It is usually a result of alterations in the calcium phosphate metabolism. Normally, the calcium phosphate maintains electrolytes in an insoluble state. As the renal glomerular filtrate rate decreases, phosphate stops being excreted by the kidneys. Calcium complexes form and are deposited in various parts of the body. This is referred to as metastatic calcification. Low calcium stimulates a rise in parathyroid hormone secretion, which causes bone re-absorption of calcium. This eventually leads to demineralisation of the bones and elevated alkaline phosphates level. In children the disease resembles rickets and in adults it resembles osteomalacia.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers

Bishops Computers</p>
<p>The Mechanism of Renal Osteodystrophy</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-7b3b05e1.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Growth retardation</li>
<li>Muscle weakness</li>
<li>Bone pain</li>
<li>Skeleton deformities</li>
<li>Slipped epiphyses</li>
</ul>
<p>The areas of the body most commonly affected are the joints, eyes, muscles, myocardium, lungs and blood vessels. The latter can lead to gangrene of fingers and toes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Osteomalacia, which is a lack of mineralisation of newly formed bone as a result of hypocalcaemia.</li>
<li>Ostitis fibrosa is a condition caused by re-absorption of calcium from the bone and replacement by fibrous tissue. The primary cause here is increased level of parathyroid hormone (parathormone).</li>
<li>Metastatic calcification, which results when the soft body tissues become calcified as a result of calcium phosphate deposits to these tissues.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-4-infectious-childhood-diseases">SECTION 4: INFECTIOUS CHILDHOOD DISEASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-4-infectious-childhood-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this section you shall look at the various common infectious diseases which affect children.</p>
<p>Children are more prone to infections than adults because they have low body resistance. They are also susceptible as a result of their mobility, especially as a toddler, of coming into contact with dirt and other harmful substances.</p>
<p>You will now look at the objectives for this unit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define and list the common infectious childhood diseases</li>
<li>Describe the causes and clinical features of the most common infectious childhood diseases</li>
<li>Describe the nursing care and medical management in relation to infectious childhood diseases</li>
<li>Identify possible complications that may arise</li>
</ul>

Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="meningococcal-meningitis">Meningococcal Meningitis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meningococcal-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Meningitis means inflammation of the meninges. The meninges are membranes that cover and protect the brain and spinal cord. The meninges consist of the pia mater, dura mater and the arachnoid. Causative organisms are Neisseria Meningitis (Meningococci). This micro-organism is intracellular gram negative diplococcus. There are six sero strains (groups), namely A, B, C, D, X and Y.</p>
<p>In many parts of the African continent sero group A is the main cause of epidemics. Meningococcal meningitis is the most common of the types of meningitis accounting for 90% of cases. Other types of meningitis may be caused by pneumococci or salmonella staphylococci. However viruses and mycobacterium, tubercle bacilli occasionally cause meningitis.</p>
<p>The incubation period ranges from two to ten days but commonly three to four days.</p>
<p>Meningococcal meningitis is an infectious disease that can be passed from one person to another if meningococci are present in the discharges from the nose and mouth.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-b6881015.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Normally, the meningococci are found in the nasopharynx without disturbing the host or carrier. The reservoir is mainly human. Illness results from either increased invasiveness of the bacteria or lower body resistance of the host. Some people have deficit or deficiency of some</p>
<p>gamma immunoglobulin, which in some cases runs in families. This explains why some epidemics run in the family, while other carriers show no symptoms.</p>
<p>Meningococcal meningitis is most common in children and young adults. When the surrounding blood vessels around the nasopharynx are invaded, the organisms enter the Cerebral Spinal Fluid (CSF) spreading throughout the sub-arachnoid space. This inflammatory process increases the CSF secretion in the ventricles, resulting in the interference with the CSF flow throughout the ventricular aqueducts.</p>
<p>The colour of the CSF changes according to the causative micro-organism. The cranial nerves may be affected as the infection spreads further resulting in neurological symptoms. When the CSF flow is interfered with, hydrocephalus may occur especially in infancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors-and-causes">Predisposing Factors and Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-and-causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Overcrowding and poor ventilation are the main pre-disposing factors, given that the mode of entry of micro-organisms is through inhalation. This is referred to as an exogenous type of infection. The organisms may also enter into the bloodstream through cracks in the respiratory tract in which it has been normal flora (that is endogenous infection).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="can-you-think-of-the-clinical-features-of-meningococcal-meningitis">Can you think of the clinical features of meningococcal meningitis?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#can-you-think-of-the-clinical-features-of-meningococcal-meningitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Usually the onset is acute and sudden</li>
<li>Older children may complain of a headache that becomes severe and spreads down the neck</li>
<li>The patient becomes pyrexial with tachycardia</li>
<li>Rigors are often present</li>
<li>Pain in the back and limbs</li>
<li>The patient's neck and possibly the spinal column become stiff/rigid</li>
<li>Kernig's sign is positive: patient supine with hip flexed to 90; pain and inability to fully extend the knee, Kernig's sign is negative if the patient can fully extend knee</li>
<li>Due to the fever, convulsions may occur</li>
<li>The child cries with a high-pitched voice</li>
<li>Anorexia is usually present</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 258 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>In very young babies, the anterior fontanelle may bulge outwards instead of positive Kernig's sign</li>
<li>The child is irritable, drowsy and goes into a comatose state</li>
<li>Photophobia is usually common and in some cases circulatory collapse with petechial haemorrhage may occur (bleeding spots) on the skin</li>
<li>Cyanosis and vomiting are present</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-investigations">Diagnostic Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Begin by taking the patient's personal history. A physical examination should follow.</p>
<p>A lumbar puncture is performed to analyse the CSF and may show that polymorph cells are increased. CSF is turbid in appearance (cloudy), the pressure is raised, glucose level is lower than normal and/or the amount of proteins is raised.</p>
<p>You should also investigate other suspected infections, for example, measles, malaria, typhoid, broncho-pneumonia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care-and-treatment">Nursing Care and Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient is admitted into an isolated cubicle to protect other children</li>
<li>Barrier nursing is instituted for at least the first 48 hours</li>
<li>The room should be quiet and darkened</li>
<li>Shock if present or anticipated, should be effectively managed</li>
<li>Drug therapy should be commenced at once</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="drug-therapy">Drug Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#drug-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Crystalline penicillin 300mg (500,000iu)/kg/day, ten times the normal dose given intravenously or intramuscularly three to four hourly until temperature falls, then six hourly for fourteen days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chloramphenicol (chloromycetin) can also be administered at 100mg/kg/day IM six hourly until apyrexial and general condition improves usually five to seven days then change to oral syrup for a total of fourteen days.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Phenobarbitone 5mg/kg/day tds is advised for convulsions up to 10mg tds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An ampicillin injection may be given in combination with the chloramphenicol and crystapen.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Drug dosages are determined according to each patient's individual needs, taking into consideration the age bracket.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-main-goals-of-intervention">The Main Goals of Intervention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-main-goals-of-intervention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Identify the micro-organism</li>
<li>Control the spread of infection</li>
<li>Initiate therapy immediately</li>
<li>Maintain a clear airway in a well ventilated room</li>
<li>Put up an intravenous infusion with the prescribed antibiotics</li>
<li>Maintain the fluid balance chart</li>
<li>Identify contacts in the family and elsewhere as they will require treatment also</li>
</ul>
<p>The origin of the infection should be investigated and measures taken to prevent its spread in the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-secondary-goal-how-to-prevent-complications">The Secondary Goal - How to Prevent Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-secondary-goal-how-to-prevent-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Constant and vigilant nursing assessment for increased intracranial pressure</li>
