<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Although in adults the symptoms can easily be more specific, in children they are not specific and the infection can be mistaken for other diseases. The following symptoms are acknowledged in most patients:</p>
<ul>
<li>The child complains of fever and being cold at the same time</li>
<li>The body temperature is high while shivering and sweating may be present</li>
<li>Nausea, vomiting and headache are common</li>
<li>The patient complains of painful joints, backache and general malaise</li>
<li>As the red blood cells are broken down, the child becomes anaemic and dizzy and splenomegaly and hepatomegaly may be present</li>
<li>The child generally looks sick, mentally disorientated and may display signs of pulmonary and/or cardiovascular symptoms</li>
<li>In some cases convulsions, drowsiness and even coma may occur</li>
</ul>
<p>Diagnostic Investigation</p>
<p>As a matter of routine, proper and accurate history taking and physical examinations (to include vital signs observation) should make you consider the possibility of malaria.</p>
<p>You should take blood slides to the laboratory for malarial parasite analysis. Where facilities for laboratory examinations are lacking, consider starting the child on anti-malarial therapy even if there is no fever.</p>
<p>Nursing Management</p>
<p>It is important that any child presenting with fever and other suspicious symptoms should be admitted into a ward for observation and treatment. Keep the child on bed rest in a well ventilated room then cover with a light cotton bed sheet. The patient's vital signs are taken and recorded two to four hourly. Where the temperature does not respond to anti-malarial therapy, the child should be started on a Dextrose 5% solution alternating with Darrow's solution which may be administered intravenously.</p>
<p>In many cases anti-malarial drugs are added into IV infusion. You should attend to the child's personal hygiene, paying special attention to skin and mouth care. A fluid balance chart should be strictly maintained as the child may become dehydrated if not given adequate fluids. As soon as vomiting has ceased, the patient should be given a light, well-balanced diet gradually increasing the amount as their strength returns.</p>
<p>Medical Management</p>
<p>This will vary according to whether the child comes from an endemic area. The use of chloroquine in Kenya has been discouraged because of parasitic resistance to this type of medication. The most favoured drugs now are quinine sulphate, which is administered in a dose of 10mgs/kg every eight hours orally till the blood is free of the parasites. This is followed by a single dose of sulfadoxine combined with pyrimethamine. Doses of these drugs are calculated according to the child's weight. In severe cases quinine is initially added into the infusion fluid every eight hours. When the child's condition improves, it is then given orally, as syrup.</p>
<p>Can you think of the complications that may occur if the child is not treated early and effectively?</p>
<p>Possible Complications</p>
<ul>
<li>Severe anaemia due to the destruction of red blood cells</li>
<li>Dehydration as a result of diarrhoea and/or vomiting</li>
<li>Convulsions caused by uncontrolled fever</li>
<li>Cerebral dysfunction, which may cause mental disorientation and comatose</li>
<li>Renal failure and heart failure</li>
<li>Hypoglycaemia</li>
<li>Pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Splenomegaly and hepatomegaly</li>
</ul>
<p>Paediatric Emergencies</p>
<p>There are many problems that can affect young children. These may either be deliberately or accidentally inflicted by self or others. Whatever the case, you have to be conversant with their management.</p>
<p>Where you may be unable to handle them, knowledge of the referral system for management will help.</p>
<p>The parents will similarly need assistance and support when such emergencies occur.</p>
<p>Cardio-Pulmonary Resuscitation (CPR)</p>
<p>If you find a child that has just collapsed, start resuscitation immediately using the 'ABC' approach.</p>
<p>Sequence of Actions</p>
<p>Before starting this procedure ensure both your safety and the child's. If a child is unresponsive, call for help.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>What is the 'ABC' approach for resuscitation</p>
<p>A - Airway</p>
<ul>
<li>Position the child with head back and hold jaw forward to open the airway. If neck injury is suspected use the jaw thrust method of opening the airway</li>
<li>Clear the airway of mucus or vomit with gloved fingers or suction machine if available</li>
</ul>
<p>B - Breathing</p>
<ul>
<li>Keeping the airway open, look, listen and feel for breathing, putting your face close to the child's face and looking at the chest of the child</li>
<li>If a child is not breathing provide positive pressure ventilation with a bag valve mask with 100% oxygen</li>
</ul>
<p>C - Circulation</p>
<ul>
<li>After five ventilations, if no central pulse is felt, start cardiac massage (compression) in infants, use both hands to encircle the chest, thumbs compress the sternum towards backbone about 100 times a minute</li>
</ul>
<p>Cardio-Pulmonary Resuscitation (CPR)</p>
<p>In older children, use the heel of one hand to press the lower half of the sternum toward the backbone about 100 times a minute with child lying on a firm surface.</p>
<ul>
<li>Combine lung inflation and chest compression at a ratio of 1:5</li>
<li>The force of compression should depress the chest by one third of the anterior posterior diameter</li>
<li>Continue resuscitation until child shows signs of life or help arrives</li>
<li>When more staff arrive to help, the most experienced should lead the team, and the less experienced assist</li>
<li>Try to define the cause and treat as appropriate</li>
</ul>
<p>Acute Convulsions</p>
<p>A convulsion is a spasmodic contraction of muscles. It is a very common problem among children, mostly seen in clinics and outpatient departments.</p>
<p>Can you think of the factors that might cause this condition?</p>
<p>The Most Common Causes</p>
<ul>
<li>Infections such as meningitis</li>
<li>Brain abscess</li>
<li>Malaria and other febrile conditions, which lead to infections, unrelated to the central nervous system (about 10% of children in the tropics who are seen in hospitals suffer from febrile convulsions)</li>
<li>Encephalitis</li>
<li>Otitis media</li>
<li>Congenital malformation of the central nervous system, especially hydrocephalus as well as encephalopathy post immunisation or acute infectious diseases</li>
<li>Metabolic problems such as hypocalcaemia or hypoglycaemia</li>
<li>Hypomagnesaemia</li>
<li>Water and electrolyte imbalance</li>
<li>Toxins which lead to tetanus</li>
<li>Inherited metabolic disorders such as phenylketonuria</li>
<li>Space occupying lesions like brain abscess, sub-dural haemorrhage/haematoma and brain tumour</li>
<li>Post traumatic convulsions which occur several weeks, months or even years following brain injuries</li>
<li>Systemic infections like renal diseases</li>
</ul>
<p>Diagnostic Investigations</p>
<p>History taking from the mother will ascertain when the convulsion started, the duration of fits and whether it is generalised or localised. A lumbar puncture should be taken to obtain CSF to find out the causative micro-organisms, if any. Blood chemistry tests should be performed to check the electrolyte levels and blood glucose level.</p>
<p>Take a brain scan to check for any cerebral lesions. Skull x-rays should also be taken to check for any previous head injury, especially with older children. Blood should be tested for malarial parasites and other micro-organisms in case of septicaemia. Electroencephalography may be ordered in some cases, especially in the case of uncontrollable convulsions. Blood and urine examinations should be conducted to determine ammonia level.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 272 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The child is admitted into a cubicle or side ward in a quiet environment and placed on the bed in a semi-prone position to facilitate the drainage of respiratory secretion and vomiting. Ensure that the airway is clear and the patient is breathing properly. The suction machine should be used whenever necessary. When the respiration becomes irregular, blood gases should be measured and monitored from time to time. The child should be given oxygen whenever they are cyanosed. Should the blood gases persistently be unsatisfactory, the doctor may decide to intubate and connect the patient to intermittent positive pressure ventilator. This is a mechanical method of helping the patient to breathe.</p>
<p>Any child with acute convulsions should be regularly observed with the vital signs recorded two hourly initially and gradually phased to four hourly as the condition improves. Due to pyrexia and the resultant sweating, they should be given a nourishing liquid diet and plenty of fluids at regular intervals.</p>
<p>A fluid balance chart should be maintained, paying specific attention to the urinary output. Where the patient is unable to take fluids orally, a naso-gastric tube may be inserted and used for feeding. To this end, mouth care is attended to every four hours. In order to prevent pressure sores, you should make every effort to carry out a two hourly change of position in bed. In general, daily skin care is carried out.</p>
<p>Keep a regular record of convulsions, as a means of determining the nature, frequency and duration of attacks. This is a good way of assessing whether the patient's condition is improving or not.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="burns">Burns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Small children are quite likely to get burned or scalded, as they often play close to fires and cooking pots and have not learned through experience or are yet to have the wisdom that one should not play with fire.</p>
<p>If the burn is widespread, it not only may cause a local problem but systemic complications can occur as:</p>
<ul>
<li>Large amounts of fluids are lost from the burned surface</li>
<li>Pain can also contribute to a state of shock</li>
<li>Anaemia is caused by blood loss and other causes, and secondary infection can occur</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-and-diagnostic-approach-history-taking">Clinical Features and Diagnostic Approach History Taking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-and-diagnostic-approach-history-taking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>What caused the burn?</li>
<li>When did it occur?</li>
<li>Record the date and time when the incident happened</li>
<li>Is the child epileptic?</li>
<li>What treatment has the child been given?</li>
</ul>
<p>Often you will guess how bad the burn will be when you know what caused it. Flames and electricity usually cause deeper burns than hot tea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-general-examination">A General Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-general-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Are they shocked?</li>
<li>Check the skin on their nose and fingers. If in shock, they will feel cold and will have a weak, thready pulse</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="an-examination-of-the-burn">An Examination of the Burn<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#an-examination-of-the-burn" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>How widespread is the burn? This is done using the diagram showing the different body parts and the percentage given to a burn in a specific area.</li>
<li>How deep is the burn? A blister is usually a sign of a superficial burn. Black, charred skin means a deep burn that will need grafting; so does hard skin that feels like leather. Then you must examine for signs of infection (temperature, obvious pus around the burn area).</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-5f6ad707.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg">
Burns Percentage Diagram</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 273 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diagnostic-investigations">Diagnostic Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The single most important laboratory test is the haemoglobin level (or haematocrit)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="first-aid-in-the-home">First Aid in the Home<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#first-aid-in-the-home" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If anyone gets a scald from a hot liquid or a burn from a hot object in the home the resulting damage can be minimised if the skin is cooled immediately by dipping in clean, cold water. If this is done a few seconds after the accident, it may be possible to prevent a deep burn developing. But after 10 minutes or more, it is too late.</p>
<p>The only thing that can be done is to cover the area with a clean cloth and take the child to the nearest health centre.</p>
<p>Do not encourage putting on local medicine, gentian violet, sugar, fat, sodium bicarbonate or anything else. Remember also that if burnt clothes are still in place, they are the best temporary sterile dressing and should not be removed until formal burn dressing is done.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pain-relief">Pain Relief<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pain-relief" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All patients in pain need pain relief quickly. Give IM pethidine 1mg/kg p.r.n. or morphine 0.25mg/kg p.r.n 6-hourly. Paracetamol may be sufficient in mild burns.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="restoration-of-fluid-loss">Restoration of Fluid Loss<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#restoration-of-fluid-loss" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All patients need extra fluid because fluid is lost from the burnt area. Just as in diarrhoeal disease, you may have to give an extra amount on top of the daily fluid requirements. The fluid may be given by mouth or by intravenous drip.</p>
<p>You can calculate the total fluid requirements as follows:</p>
<p>For children below 10kg, calculate using 150ml/kg body weight with a maximum of 1,000ml less than one year. Breast milk is preferred and if this is known to be sufficient you do not have to calculate at all.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="example-calculations">Example calculations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-calculations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-a-child-is-8kg-then-the-fluid-requirement-is-calculated-as">If a child is 8kg then the fluid requirement is calculated as:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-a-child-is-8kg-then-the-fluid-requirement-is-calculated-as" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Quantity is = 150ml/kg</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>If 1kg = 150mls</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>8kg = (150 x 8) = 1200mls.</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This quantity (1200mls) will therefore, be given if the child is more than one year but if less than one year of age, we give the maximum which is 1000mls.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-a-child-is-above-10kg-calculate-as-follows-for-a-child-between-11-and-20kg-1-000ml-50ml-kg-for-every-kg-above-10kg">If a child is above 10kg, calculate as follows: - For a child between 11 and 20kg: 1,000ml + (50ml/kg for every kg above 10kg)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-a-child-is-above-10kg-calculate-as-follows-for-a-child-between-11-and-20kg-1-000ml-50ml-kg-for-every-kg-above-10kg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For example: If the child weighs 15kg, amount of fluid given is:</p>
<p>1000ml + (50ml/kg for every kg above 10kg - here, 5 from 15-10kg)</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable rowspacing="0.16em" columnalign="left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1000</mn><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>50</mn><mtext>&nbsp;ml</mtext><mo></mo><mn>5</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1000</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>250</mn></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1250</mn><mtext>&nbsp;mls&nbsp;as&nbsp;the&nbsp;fluid&nbsp;given&nbsp;to&nbsp;the&nbsp;child</mtext></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mtext>weighing&nbsp;15kg</mtext></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\begin{array}{l}
= 1000 + (50 \text{ ml} \times 5) \\
= 1000 + 250 \\
= 1250 \text{ mls as the fluid given to the child} \\
\text{weighing 15kg}
\end{array}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 4.8em; vertical-align: -2.15em;"></span><span <div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="for-a-child-above-20kg-1-500ml-plus-20-ml-kg-for-every-kg-above-20kg">For a child above 20kg: 1,500ml plus 20 ml/kg for every kg above 20kg<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#for-a-child-above-20kg-1-500ml-plus-20-ml-kg-for-every-kg-above-20kg" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For example: If the child weighs 25kg, amount of fluid given is:</p>
<p>1500ml + (20ml/kg for every kg above 20kg - here, 5 from 25-20kg)</p>
<div class="math math-display"><span class="katex-display"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block"><semantics><mtable rowspacing="0.16em" columnalign="left" columnspacing="1em"><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1500</mn><mo>+</mo><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>20</mn><mtext>&nbsp;ml</mtext><mo></mo><mn>5</mn><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1500</mn><mo>+</mo><mn>100</mn></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mrow><mo>=</mo><mn>1600</mn><mtext>&nbsp;mls&nbsp;as&nbsp;the&nbsp;fluid&nbsp;given&nbsp;to&nbsp;the&nbsp;child</mtext></mrow></mstyle></mtd></mtr><mtr><mtd><mstyle scriptlevel="0" displaystyle="false"><mtext>weighing&nbsp;15kg</mtext></mstyle></mtd></mtr></mtable><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\begin{array}{l}
= 1500 + (20 \text{ ml} \times 5) \\
= 1500 + 100 \\
= 1600 \text{ mls as the fluid given to the child} \\
\text{weighing 15kg}
\end{array}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 4.8em; vertical-align: -2.15em;"></span><span 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mord">1500</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">20</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;ml</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin"></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span><span style="top: -3.61em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mord">1500</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">+</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mord">100</span></span></span><span style="top: -2.41em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mord">1600</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;mls&nbsp;as&nbsp;the&nbsp;fluid&nbsp;given&nbsp;to&nbsp;the&nbsp;child</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -1.21em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">weighing&nbsp;15kg</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s"></span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 2.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="arraycolsep" style="width: 0.5em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></div>
<p>The above are administered orally.</p>
<p>20ml/kg has to be added for every 10% of body surface or part burned.</p>
<p>To complete the total required, you add this to the already calculated value as the table fluid replacement shows.</p>
<p>Fluid Replacement Table</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>% of body surface burned</th><th>Extra fluids to be given (ml/kg)</th><th>Type of fluid and how given</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>10 or less</td><td>20</td><td>Can be given as homemade electrolyte solution by mouth</td></tr><tr><td>20</td><td>40</td><td>IV saline or preferably Ringer's Lactate</td></tr><tr><td>30</td><td>60</td><td>Ideally every other bottle should be plasma</td></tr><tr><td>40</td><td>80</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>50</td><td>100</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>For example, using the above example of the last calculation done:</p>
<p>If a child weighing 25kg with a 20% burn, the child has to receive fluid replacement totalling to: Resuscitation amount = 1600mls as calculated above</p>
<p>For 20% burns = 40ml/kg
1kg = 40ml
so, 25kg = (25 X 40) = 1000mls.</p>
<p>Therefore the total fluid requirements = 1600mls + 1000mls = 2600mls of fluid</p>
<p>The method used for this is oral for the 1600mls then as shown in the table, intravenous for the 1000mls.</p>
<p>To administer the amount of fluid given in relation to the % of the burn, the table offers the guide.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="local-treatment">Local Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#local-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>While the pethidine or morphine is working, gently wash the burned area with warm soapy water, remove any dirt or dead skin and gently dry. For burns of the body, limbs, genitals, face and neck, you want the air to get to the area to dry it out, so use no dressings or medicines. This is called exposure treatment. A bed cradle keeps the bedclothes off the area.</p>
<p>For burns of the hands and feet, closed treatment is better. This means that after washing, you put on white petroleum jelly (Vaseline) or Vaseline gauze if you have it, then bandage the limb in a functional position and elevate it on pillows or in a sling. Each finger should be bandaged separately. The burns are soaked in warm, soapy water every day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-burns">Treatment of Burns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="antibacterial-treatment">Antibacterial Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antibacterial-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Although sterile techniques are essential, you cannot prevent the burn from becoming infected, even if broad-spectrum antibiotics are given.</p>
<p>You can, however, prevent streptococcal infection which may result in erysipelas, glomerulonephritis or rheumatic fever by giving penicillin (PPF 400,000 units daily). Tetanus prophylaxis is indicated. If not vaccinated, give ATS 1,500 units after testing and start tetanus immunisation.</p>
<p>If vaccinated more than two years ago, boost with tetanus toxoid 0.5ml stat IM.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-of-anaemia">Treatment of Anaemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-of-anaemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Keep a check once weekly on the haemoglobin. Give a blood transfusion if it falls below 7g/dl in the first week. Give a course of ferrous sulphate for less severe anaemia.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="transfer-to-hospital">Transfer to Hospital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#transfer-to-hospital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Transfer all severe burns to centres with experienced staff and special facilities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="severe-burns">Severe Burns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#severe-burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Extensive burns (more than 25% of body area)</li>
<li>Deep burns or burns that have not healed in 14-17 days</li>
<li>Flame burns to the face and eyelids</li>
<li>Contractures following untreated burns</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="poisoning">Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="poisoning">Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are different types of poisoning. Ingested poisoning includes the ingestion of alcohol, organophosphates, kerosene and common drugs, for example, aspirin. Inhaled poisoning may include the inhalation of carbon monoxide, ethanol and organophosphates.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Identification of poisoning includes taking a detailed history which includes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Examining the drugs available at home or noting drug containers/bottles found nearby</li>
<li>Recording the place where ingestion or inhalation took place</li>
<li>Analysing any vomitus or urine saved</li>
</ul>
<p>Poisons create different effects on the body, which range from symptomatic changes to clinical changes then metabolic changes. These effects include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Vomiting and haematemesis</li>
<li>Convulsions or involuntary movement</li>
<li>Oculogyric spasms</li>
<li>Hallucinations and agitation</li>
<li>Pupils either dilated or constricted</li>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Respiratory failure</li>
<li>Cardiac failure</li>
<li>Hypoglycaemia</li>
<li>Metabolic acidosis</li>
<li>Stupor/coma</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This will depend on the type of poison taken by the child, the time span since it was taken and the route of intake. Some poisons have antidotes and some do not. The place where the patient is being cared for will also be of great importance because of the availability of the equipment supplies and qualified personnel.</p>
<p>Some of the general actions, which can be taken in the management of poisons, include the removal of poisons from the body if these are known. This involves provoking vomiting (emesis) with the fingers for non-corrosive and non-inhalant ingested poisons. Ipecacuanha syrup may be used instead of the above. This is given as a dose of 15mls stat orally, followed by 200mls of water. Wait for 15-20 minutes for the patient to vomit. If there is no vomiting, repeat with a dose of 15mls orally and wait for 20 minutes. If the patient still has not vomited, perform gastric lavage.</p>
<p>The blood should be tested for the poisonous substance taken by the child if known and an intravenous infusion using Darrow's solution of 50% Dextrose may be given to correct hypoglycaemia. Oxygen therapy can be administered where necessary. The child should be given oral alkaline fluids to neutralise the acid and vice versa. Urinary catheterisation is indicated in order to monitor urinary output when renal failure is suspected.</p>
<p>The patient's general condition should be assessed to include level of consciousness and inspection of the mouth and lips for any burns in case of corrosive poisoning. Neurological investigations should also be undertaken.</p>
<p>You will look at kerosene poisoning and insecticide poisoning specifically</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kerosene-paraffin-poisoning">Kerosene (Paraffin) Poisoning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kerosene-paraffin-poisoning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Young children often drink kerosene by accident. It is kept in the houses as fuel for lamps or primus stoves and is often kept in an old juice, soda or beer bottle. A child will usually not drink more than a mouthful because of the unpleasant taste.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main danger lies in aspiration into the lungs, causing bronchopneumonia. For this reason, vomiting is dangerous and should never be induced. The kerosene also can cause acute pulmonary oedema. Another immediate effect may be coma due to narcotic effect of kerosene.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Do not induce vomiting and do not wash out the stomach</li>
<li>Give 5ml of milk of magnesia as a laxative instead</li>
<li>Pneumonia is such a common complication that it pays to start pneumonia treatment immediately</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insecticide-poisoning-parathion-malathion">Insecticide Poisoning (Parathion, Malathion)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insecticide-poisoning-parathion-malathion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Contact with these poisons causes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Tremors of the muscles</li>
<li>Sweating</li>
<li>Copious secretion of the saliva</li>
<li>Pinpoint pupils</li>
</ul>
<p>In the later stages it causes:</p>
<ul>
<li>Convulsions</li>
<li>Coma and/or paralysis</li>
</ul>
<p>The pinpoint pupils can help you make this diagnosis and guide you in the treatment. The treatment consists of first washing the child with soap and water, if there has been skin exposure, then giving them very large doses of atropine intramuscularly - in children under five, 0.5mg and in older children 1mg atropine sulphate IM every 15-30 minutes, until the pupils become wide.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Note that these dangerously high doses of atropine are indicated only in a serious case of confirmed insecticide poisoning. Referral may then be done if appears necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preventive-measures">Preventive Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preventive-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Children at the age of five years and below should always be protected from injuries or accidental poisoning wherever they may be. After the age of five years they are educated to distinguish between what is right and wrong and dangerous.</p>
<p>Adults, especially parents, should not experiment the use of certain substances in the presence of children because children are bound to try and imitate them. You should find out from the parents how the accidental poisoning occurred in order to give the correct and effective health education on the topic.</p>
<p>All petroleum products should be kept safely locked and in their correct containers. All drugs in the home should be securely locked away out of children's reach. Parents should always be given health education on preventive measures, the dangers of poisoning and first aid measures to be taken in case of poisoning for their children.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="child-abuse-neglect">Child Abuse/Neglect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#child-abuse-neglect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Health care workers especially doctors, nurses and social workers must be on the lookout at all times during their clinical practice for signs of child abuse or neglect. Although these problems are known to exist in the world, incidence has increased in terms of numbers and frequency. Additionally, societies have become more open and it is now easier to expose cases of child abuse than ever before. The media have been increasingly vocal in pointing out incidents of child abuse.</p>
<p>The health care worker must be constantly vigilant to be able to detect, investigate and report to the rightful authorities so that remedial activities can be taken before further injuries are inflicted to the helpless children. It may be argued by some that certain activities affecting children are merely cultural practices carried out in some African traditional societies to maintain their way of life. The problem is that the children's consent has never been sought.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-children-s-rights">Basic Children's Rights<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-children-s-rights" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The United Nations has come up with a list of basic children's rights, which should be observed and protected, by all world member countries. They are summarised as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>The right to live</li>
<li>The right to acquire a name and nationality</li>
<li>The right to enjoy parental care</li>
<li>The right to proper food and health care</li>
<li>The right to education</li>
<li>The right to be protected from all kinds of harm</li>
<li>The right to moral upbringing</li>
<li>The right to a culture</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-child-abuse-and-neglect">Types of Child Abuse and Neglect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-child-abuse-and-neglect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are different types of child abuse and neglect, including physical abuse, neglect and abandonment, sexual abuse, emotional and psychological abuse. Nutritional abuse can well be incorporated within one of the first four. These abuses may occur singly or in combination. The different types of abuse will now be covered in more detail.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="physical-abuse-battered-baby-syndrome-or-battered-child-syndrome">Physical Abuse (battered baby syndrome or battered child syndrome)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#physical-abuse-battered-baby-syndrome-or-battered-child-syndrome" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the most common form of child abuse, which is easily recognised by health care workers and lay persons alike. The child displays non-accidental injuries on their body. The majority of victims in this group are infants or pre-school children. About 60-70% are below three years old in Europe and America, while in Africa the age goes up to five years. The child's behaviour is abnormal, demanding too much attention, behaving aggressively or withdrawn. The child may have a chronic illness or be physically disabled. Some of these children may belong to single mothers who had unwanted or unplanned pregnancies and are unable to cope with the strains of motherhood.</p>
<p>Various types of injuries may be observed. These include burns, cigarette burns, cuts, bruises, lacerations, fractures and bites. Some of these injuries may be in the healing stage while others may be fresh. This is an indication of repeatedly inflicted injuries. Injuries are predominantly seen in the genital areas,</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>buttocks, back, limbs, face. Ruptured internal abdominal organs and fractured skull may also be identified.</p>
<p>Physical abusers may include individuals suffering from stress, alcoholics, mentally ill individuals, those who were themselves battered in childhood or drug addicts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-might-you-manage-a-child-that-has-suffered-physical-abuse">How might you manage a child that has suffered physical abuse?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-might-you-manage-a-child-that-has-suffered-physical-abuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Once child abuse is detected or suspected, the child should be removed to a safer environment and involve the health care worker and children's departments. The child needs to be hospitalised in order to undergo a thorough physical and mental assessment to detect other previous injuries that may have been sustained. This detection is necessary in case of legal action being taken against the person who inflicted the injuries on the child.</p>
<p>When a child is admitted to hospital, an x-ray, physical examination, medical or surgical treatment should be carried out as appropriate.</p>
<p>The parents or guardians will require counselling especially if they are the ones causing injury to the child. The child's nutritional status should be improved before being transferred to a children's home or a foster home. These transfers are usually undertaken with the approval of the court of law, the Children's Department and Probation Office.</p>
<p>It is recommended that the offenders or abusers undergo corrective measures instead of a punitive corrective approach. Many, if not all, are referred to psychiatrists for assessment and assistance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="child-neglect-and-abandonment">Child Neglect and Abandonment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#child-neglect-and-abandonment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In African societies, this problem was unheard of until a few decades ago. This problem has been brought about by social changes, which have led to the gradual erosion of extended family ties. Children who are abandoned are usually malnourished and may have other diseases as a result of low resistance to infection.</p>
<p>A great number of factors have contributed to this social problem in developing countries. Often both parents are economically unable to meet their basic needs due to poverty. Additionally, some children are brought up by single parents, who may not be able to earn enough to support their family. Perhaps the problem originates from the death of a spouse or a divorce, which leaves the remaining partner unable to provide for the family.</p>
<p>The children of physically and mentally handicapped mothers may be abandoned if they are unable to cope with the demands of motherhood. In certain conditions, a child may be separated from the mother for a prolonged period as a result of imprisonment. Similar problems may also be noted when a mother is an alcoholic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-neglected-and-abandoned-children">Management of Neglected and Abandoned Children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-neglected-and-abandoned-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A child needs love, accommodation and food. You should make an effort to provide these in the health care facility while arrangements are being made to provide a suitable home for the child outside the hospital environment. Apart from these, medical treatment is provided as appropriate.</p>
<p>You shall now move on to the last sub-section, which will assist you in managing children in the unit or rural health centres.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foreign-bodies-in-orifices">Foreign Bodies in Orifices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foreign-bodies-in-orifices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="foreign-bodies-in-orifices">Foreign Bodies in Orifices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foreign-bodies-in-orifices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Children tend to insert foreign bodies into their orifices during play. Unaware of the consequences of their actions, they become victims of injuries or diseases. The problem occurs most often in toddlers and slightly older children when they are left unattended.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-b371ccf3.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg">
Foreign Bodies in the Respiratory Tract</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Infants and toddlers between the age of six months and three years are the most common victims of foreign bodies in the respiratory tract. Some may remove the foreign bodies by the reflex action of coughing, but in certain cases these objects remain stuck. The clinical manifestation may be immediate or delayed depending on the level of the airway where the object is stuck and the size of the foreign body. Should the object be large, the child could become asphyxiated within three to five minutes. The pathophysiological effects produced by aspirating or pushing foreign bodies into the respiratory tract are generally dependent on three main things, that is, the nature or composition of the foreign object, anatomical sites where the object is lodged and the degree of the respiratory obstruction.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-clinical-features-do-you-think-the-child-may-display">What clinical features do you think the child may display?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-clinical-features-do-you-think-the-child-may-display" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Foreign body may be visible on examination</li>
<li>The child feels uncomfortable and may attempt to sneeze</li>
<li>Nasal mucosa becomes irritable and swollen</li>
<li>Local obstruction of the nostril may be evident</li>
<li>Some objects like beans and maize will definitely swell after absorbing moisture or water, this worsens the situation further</li>
<li>Infective purulent nasal discharge may occur especially if the foreign body is left inside for a prolonged period of time</li>
<li>Cough, hoarseness and inability to talk or cry properly</li>
<li>Wheezy respiration leading to dyspnoea and cyanosis leading to choking or suffocation</li>
<li>Child becomes anxious and restless</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-investigations">Diagnostic Investigations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-investigations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Investigations include history taking from the parents or any one who may have seen what actually happened.</p>
<p>A physical examination should include an X-ray to examine the larynx, trachea and chest in general. A Laryngoscopy or bronchoscopy may also be performed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is an emergency situation, which must be handled with speed and efficiency if the child is to be saved. During a laryngoscopy and/or bronchoscopy, the visible foreign objects may be removed by using forceps or sucked out if they are in liquid form. Some objects can easily be removed by applying first aid technique.</p>
<p>For example, a piece of meat in the airway may be quickly removed by holding the child upside down (legs up and head downwards) then thumbing the posterior chest a number of times. This in most cases dislodges the object straight away. In case of liquids, suction may be quite sufficient to clear the respiratory tract thereby improving breathing.</p>
<p>The doctor will perform a laryngoscopy or bronchoscopy to investigate and remove visible foreign bodies from the airway using long forceps or a sucker depending on the type of foreign body. After removal, the child may be given oxygen for a while to improve his general condition. The child and their parents are reassured. If the objects have gone too deep into the lower respiratory tract and cannot be removed then a thoracotomy is performed under general anaesthesia followed by lobectomy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nursing-care">Nursing Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The patient is kept in hospital for a few days of observations if the foreign body is removed without surgery. If surgery is performed, the duration of hospitalisation is prolonged because of the need for intensive nursing care. Antibiotics are prescribed for possible complication such as pneumonia, which may follow the trauma caused by the foreign body. Analgesics are also recommended.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foreign-bodies-in-the-ear">Foreign Bodies in the Ear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foreign-bodies-in-the-ear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Children may push or insert a foreign body into the external auditory canal. In some cases, these foreign bodies so lodged stay inside until a pathological change takes place causing additional discomfort to the child.</p>
<p>When the object is visible, it may be removed with a forceps, blunt cerumen curet or a wire loop. Whichever method is used, the child has to co-operate or be restrained if the treatment has to be successful. Depending on the type of</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>foreign body, the ear may have to be irrigated using warm water or normal saline provided the tympanic membrane is intact. Where the foreign body is either a bean or a pea, contact with water should not be allowed because it may swell, making the removal rather difficult.</p>
<p>Otomicroscopy may be performed under general anaesthesia to remove the foreign body after which the tympanic membrane is carefully inspected for any traumatic perforation or inflammation. Thereafter, eardrops may be instilled as necessary.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="foreign-bodies-in-the-eye">Foreign Bodies in the Eye<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foreign-bodies-in-the-eye" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Research has shown that approximately 10% of all bodily injuries involve the eyes and more single-eye loss from trauma occurs during the first ten years of life than in any other time (Harley, 1983). It follows, therefore, that more children of about two years of age and above suffer from traumas, which may lead to blindness.</p>
<p>Foreign bodies in the children's eyes usually include soil, sand, insects, and chemicals. The patient presents with painful irritation of the affected eye, lacrimation, photophobia and closure of the eye. The foreign body may be visible on careful inspection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Initially, the management is mostly first aid, which may be followed by conservation treatment and nursing care. The child should be kept still, supported and reassured. The parents should be similarly reassured and instructed on</p>
<p>what to do while arrangements for referral is being made. Loose particles in the eye may be removed with wet gauze and little restraining. The patient's eye may be irrigated using warm water or mild solution of normal saline. In the hospital casualty department, or in the ward, a pad or eye shield is placed in situ loosely especially when additional medical treatment is considered necessary. Thereafter, the management depends on the type of foreign body and extent of injury.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In all cases of accidents with children, however trivial, the parents require sympathy and a kind approach as they often feel guilty and bear the blame. The nurses should offer health education and refrain from criticism. Parents should be advised to ensure adults supervise the children as much as possible. Dangerous objects need to be removed from the playgrounds and venues as a preventive measure. It goes without saying that emphasis should also be made on the parents to urgently take their children to hospital once such unfortunate states of affair occur and not be dissuaded from doing so by the attendant feelings of fear or guilt.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 279 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>UNIT FOUR PART TWO: PAEDIATRIC NURSING 2</p>
<p>In this unit, you are going to cover diseases and conditions, which commonly affect children up to the age of twelve years.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define each common childhood disease</li>
<li>List the causes and predisposing factors of each condition/disease</li>
<li>State the clinical features and investigations to be conducted for each condition/disease</li>
<li>Describe the management of children with any of the conditions/diseases mentioned</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-respiratory-tract-dysfunctions">SECTION 1: RESPIRATORY TRACT DYSFUNCTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-respiratory-tract-dysfunctions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>As you prepare to study these conditions in depth, you should bear in mind that the management of sick children extends beyond the hospital ward boundaries into the home, community and school.</p>
<p>Nursing of children should not be carried out in isolation. Their care must be related to their environment. Therefore, you must try to work in liaison with the child's parents, community members and other relevant professionals concerned in child care to achieve set objectives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define and list the common respiratory tract diseases</li>
<li>State their causes and clinical features</li>
<li>Describe the nursing care and medical management in relation to respiratory tract diseases</li>
<li>Identify possible complications that may arise</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="acute-bronchitis-tracheobronchitis">Acute Bronchitis (Tracheobronchitis)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#acute-bronchitis-tracheobronchitis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is an acute inflammation of one or more bronchi in children, which affects those below the age of four years. The infection is more prevalent in the younger children than</p>
<p>the older ones because the former group have low resistance. Although referred to as bronchitis, the trachea, which is anatomically and physiologically related to the bronchi cannot escape infection when the latter is involved.</p>
<p>The disease is always associated with the upper respiratory tract infections, caused by various types of micro-organisms such as the influenza virus, streptococci, and pneumococci. In some cases, it is associated with certain communicable or infectious diseases such as whooping cough, measles and typhoid fever, just to name a few.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-b0dabb1d.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<p>Acute bronchitis may present itself as a mild or severe manifestation. It frequently attacks malnourished and debilitated children from overcrowded homes. Environmental air pollution, allergic conditions and climatic changes, especially cold months and housing may precipitate the condition. Some young children with congenital heart defects or fibrocystic disease of the pancreas also tend to develop acute bronchitis due to their low immunity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="clinical-features">Clinical Features<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>When you receive a child with acute bronchitis in your area of work, they may present with certain symptoms.</p>
<p> Generally weak and unwell</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Page 280 of 425</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p> Their cheeks and skin may be flushed and their mouth may be dry
 Have dyspnoea leading to restlessness and irritability
 On checking the vital signs, the child will be pyrexial with temperature running between 39 and 40 degrees Celsius, in some cases even above these figures
 The respiration, though increased, is usually shallow due to pleural pain
 Older children normally complain of anterior chest pain, which may increase with frequent coughing at first
 Later on, the cough may become productive and the patient will be exhausted as a result of the above symptoms</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Unless the condition is severe, hospitalisation may not be necessary. The child can be treated and managed as an outpatient under the care of the parents.</p>
<p>Should hospitalisation be required, the child should be admitted in a cubicle and barrier nursed. The environment should be kept warm, humidified and well ventilated until the medical personnel are sure the patient does not have any communicable disease. Bed rest should be maintained until their temperature returns to normal. Their vital signs of temperature, pulse and respiration are taken and recorded one to two hourly.</p>
<p>Mechanical methods of lowering the body temperature should be employed as found fit. These include electric fanning or reduction of extra bed clothing. The child can adopt any comfortable position they like. Oxygen administration is given when necessary via a ventimask for older children and a tent for younger ones. Oxygen should be humidified.</p>
